       <p>In this tutorial we are going to learn how to create a simple MVC application using servlets and jsp.</p> 
       <p>MVC i.e. Model-View-Controller is a pattern helpful separation of concerns.</p> 
       <ul> 
        <li>Model represents a POJO object that carries data.</li> 
        <li>View is the layer in which the data is presented in visual format.</li> 
        <li>Controller is the component which is responsible for communication between model and view.</li> 
       </ul> 
       <p>A user always sees the view and communicates with the controller. We will understand this using a sample login application which will display a welcome username message and if the login fails, it will redirect to an error page. Here is what we are going to create.</p> 
       <ul> 
        <li>login.jsp :- this will input username and password</li> 
        <li>success.jsp :- If login is successful, then this page is displayed</li> 
        <li>error.jsp :- If login is not successful then this page is displayed.</li> 
        <li>LoginController.java :- This is controller part of the application which communicates with model</li> 
        <li>Authenticator.java :- Has business logic for authentication</li> 
        <li>User.java :- Stores username and password for the user.</li> 
       </ul> 
       <p>Requirements:</p> 
       <ul> 
        <li>Eclipse IDE</li> 
        <li>Apache tomcat server</li> 
        <li>JSTL jar</li> 
       </ul> 
       <ol> 
        <ol>
         Create a new Dynamic web project in eclipse by clicking File -&gt; New -&gt; Dynamic Web Project. Fill the details i.e. project name, the server. Enter your project name as MVCDemo. You will get the following directory structure for the project.
        </ol> 
       </ol> 
       <div id="attachment_207" style="width: 280px" class="wp-caption alignnone">
        <a href="http://www.thejavageek.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/ProjectStructure.jpg"><img class="size-full wp-image-207" alt="Initial Project Structure" src="http://www.thejavageek.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/ProjectStructure.jpg" width="270" height="128" srcset="http://www.thejavageek.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/ProjectStructure.jpg 270w, http://www.thejavageek.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/ProjectStructure-260x123.jpg 260w, http://www.thejavageek.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/ProjectStructure-160x75.jpg 160w" sizes="(max-width: 270px) 100vw, 270px"></a>
        <p class="wp-caption-text">Initial Project Structure</p>
       </div>

         Create success.jsp, error.jsp and login.jsp and LoginController servlet, Authenticator class, User class in the packages as shown in the images. Put the jstl.jar in WEB-INF/lib folder.
        </ol> 
       </ol>

        <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
         <textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
package mvcdemo.controllers;

import java.io.IOException;

import javax.servlet.RequestDispatcher;
import javax.servlet.ServletException;
import javax.servlet.http.HttpServlet;
import javax.servlet.http.HttpServletRequest;
import javax.servlet.http.HttpServletResponse;

import mvcdemo.model.Authenticator;
import mvcdemo.model.User;

import sun.text.normalizer.ICUBinary.Authenticate;

public class LoginController extends HttpServlet {
	private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L;

	public LoginController() {
		super();
	}

	protected void doPost(HttpServletRequest request,
			HttpServletResponse response) throws ServletException, IOException {

		String username = request.getParameter("username");
		String password = request.getParameter("password");
		RequestDispatcher rd = null;

		Authenticator authenticator = new Authenticator();
		String result = authenticator.authenticate(username, password);
		if (result.equals("success")) {
			rd = request.getRequestDispatcher("/success.jsp");
			User user = new User(username, password);
			request.setAttribute("user", user);
		} else {
			rd = request.getRequestDispatcher("/error.jsp");
		}
		rd.forward(request, response);
	}

}</textarea>
        </div>

package mvcdemo.model;

public class Authenticator {

	public String authenticate(String username, String password) {
		if (("prasad".equalsIgnoreCase(username))
				&amp;&amp; ("password".equals(password))) {
			return "success";
		} else {
			return "failure";
		}
	}
}</textarea>

package mvcdemo.model;

public class User {

	private String username;
	private String password;

	public User(String username, String password){
		this.username = username;
		this.password = password;
	}

	public String getUsername() {
		return username;
	}

	public void setUsername(String username) {
		this.username = username;
	}

	public String getPassword() {
		return password;
	}

	public void setPassword(String password) {
		this.password = password;
	}

}</textarea>

       <!-- [Format Time: 0.0034 seconds] --> 
       <p>We are done with the code. Let us try and run it.</p> 
       <p>Start your tomcat server and hit url <a title="http://localhost:8080/MVCDemo/login.jsp" href="http://localhost:8080/MVCDemo/login.jsp">http://localhost:8080/MVCDemo/login.jsp.</a></p> 
       <p>You should be able to view this page.</p> 
       <p><a href="http://www.thejavageek.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/loginForm.jpg"><img class="alignnone size-medium wp-image-210" alt="loginForm" src="http://www.thejavageek.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/loginForm-300x81.jpg" width="300" height="81" srcset="http://www.thejavageek.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/loginForm-300x81.jpg 300w, http://www.thejavageek.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/loginForm-260x70.jpg 260w, http://www.thejavageek.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/loginForm-160x43.jpg 160w, http://www.thejavageek.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/loginForm.jpg 320w" sizes="(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px"></a></p> 
       <p>Enter username as prasad and password as password. You will see the message Welcome prasad.</p> 
       <p>Let us understand what happens under the hood with the help of diagram.</p> 
       <p><a href="http://www.thejavageek.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/MVCFlow1.jpg"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-213" alt="MVCFlow" src="http://www.thejavageek.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/MVCFlow1.jpg" width="645" height="371" srcset="http://www.thejavageek.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/MVCFlow1.jpg 645w, http://www.thejavageek.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/MVCFlow1-300x172.jpg 300w, http://www.thejavageek.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/MVCFlow1-560x322.jpg 560w, http://www.thejavageek.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/MVCFlow1-260x149.jpg 260w, http://www.thejavageek.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/MVCFlow1-160x92.jpg 160w" sizes="(max-width: 645px) 100vw, 645px"></a></p> 
       <ol> 
        <li>First, user visits login.jsp page and fills out data and submits form.</li> 
        <li>This causes&nbsp; <span id="crayon-59beca8575ce4787516800" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">LoginController</span></span></span>&nbsp; to be invoked because of <span id="crayon-59beca8575ce7726440642" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;">form<span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e ">action</span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-s ">"LoginController"</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span></span></span></li> 
        <li>In <span id="crayon-59beca8575cea261408770" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;">LoginController</span></span> , following code causes the model to be invoked and set the <span id="crayon-59beca8575ced485280961" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;">User</span></span> properties.<br>

          </div> 
         </div> 
         <!-- [Format Time: 0.0005 seconds] --> <br> and <span id="crayon-59beca8575cf4395654894" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-e">User </span><span class="crayon-v">user</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">new</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">User</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-v">username</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">password</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></span></span> .</li> 
        <li> <span id="crayon-59beca8575cf6992507951" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">rd</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-e">forward</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-v">request</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">response</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></span></span> causes the servlet to forward to jsp page.</li> 
       </ol> 
       <p>success.jsp page displays the username with expression language <span id="crayon-59beca8575cf9414918013" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;">Welcome<span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">$</span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span>requestScope<span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-s ">'user'</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span>username<span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span></span></span></p> 
       <p>Notable advantages of mvc pattern are:</p> 
       <ul> 
        <li>This separate presentation layer from business layer.</li> 
        <li>The controller performs action of invoking the model and sending data to view.</li> 
        <li>Model is not even aware that it is used by some web application or desktop application. Authenticator class can be used by desktop applications also. Thus separation helps in re-usability.</li> 
       </ul> 
       <p>Hope this helps in understanding how to create MVC application using servlets and jsp.</p>

            <div class="comment-meta">
              November 23, 2013 at 1:03 am 
            </div> 
            <div class="comment-text"> 
             <p>I would recommend you to take up a sample project and implement it using MVC architecture so that you will get to know the difficulties faced during development. For example, create a simple user registration form in which fields are entered on a JSP, access them in a servlet and again display the list of all registered users on a separate JSP page. Use MVC architecture in it.</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="reply"> 
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.thejavageek.com/2013/08/11/mvc-architecture-with-servlets-and-jsp/?replytocom=9841#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-9841&quot;, &quot;9841&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;204&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Prasad Kharkar">Reply</a>

            <div class="comment-text"> 
             <p>1. Though you are using netbeans, it may have a different directory structure, so instead of webcontent directory, it can have other one. The rules for a web application do not change. You just need to create a dynamic web project in netbeans and follow the process given in this tutorial<br> 2. You will have to use file upload functionality for uploading photo and while displaying, I recommend you simply store the uploaded photo on hard drive and put the location of photo in database. While displaying photo for profile, you can pick photo location from database and display on web page. </p> 
             <p>I will certainly write more tutorials as per your suggestion ? Thank you for reading a positive feedback. Happy learning.</p>

          <div class="comment-text"> 
           <p>Great tutorial, just one error. On the jsp file the line</p> 
           <p>Welcome ${requestScope[user].username}</p> 
           <p>should be</p> 
           <p>Welcome ${requestScope[user].getUsername()} </p> 
           <p>because your attribute is private and you have a getter for it</p> 
          </div>

            <div class="comment-text"> 
             <p>Hi Ashish, jsps are meant for displaying purpose only. a JSP developer need not have knowledge of sql queries. Writing sql or java code in jsp would break the mvc pattern. It is not advisable to write logic in jsp. You should use servlet or further layers to call values from database.</p> 
            </div>
